باب المحرمات
وحَرُمَ على المرء أصله وفرعُه ، وأخته وبنتها ، وبنت أخيه، وعمته وخالته ،
وبنت زوجته إن وطئت
واعلم أن المحرمات أنواع :
الأول : المحرمات بالنسب.
والنوع الثاني : المحرمات بالمصاهرة، وهو أنواع أربعة.
والنوع الثالث : المحرمات بالرضاع.
والنوع الرابع : حرمة الجمع.
والنوع الخامس : الحرمة بحق الغير كمنكوحة الغير ومعتدته.
والنوع السادس : المحرمة لعدم دين سماوي.
والنوع السابع : المحرمة للتنافي كنكاح السيدة مملوكها.
الأصلُ في تحريم هذه المذكورات قوله تعالى: (حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمْ أُمَّهَاتُكُمْ وَبَنَاتُكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُمْ وَعَمَّاتُكُمْ وَخَالَاتُكُمْ وَبَنَاتُ الْأَخِ وَبَنَاتُ الْأُخْتِ وَأُمَّهَاتُكُمُ الَّتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُم مِّنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ وَأُمَّهَاتُ نِسَائِكُمْ وَرَبَائِبُكُمُ الَّتِي فِي حُجُورِكُم مِّن نِّسَائِكُمُ الَّتِي دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ فَإِن لَّمْ تَكُونُوا دَخَلْتُم بِهِنَّ فَلَا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَحَلَائِلُ أَبْنَائِكُمُ الَّذِينَ مِنْ أَصْلَابِكُمْ وَأَن تَجْمَعُوا بَيْنَ الْأُخْتَيْنِ إِلَّا مَا قَدْ سَلَفَ إِنَّ اللهَ كَانَ غَفُورًا رَّحِيمًا) (وَالْمُحْصَنَاتُ مِنَ النِّسَاءِ إِلَّا مَا مَلَكَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ).
وقال قبيل هذه الآية: ﴿ وَلَا تَنكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ آبَاؤُكُم مِّنَ النِّسَاءِ ﴾،
والمراد بالأمهات ما يشمل الجدّات من قبل الأم أو من قبل الأب إجماعاً، وتشمل لفظ البنات البنات الصلبية وبنات الابن وبنات البنت، وإن سلفت.
وألحق بالعمات والخالات عمات الأب والأم وخالاتهما، وكذا عمات الجد والجدة وخالتهما، ودلّ إطلاقهما وإطلاق الأخوات وغيرها على عموم الحرمة في جميع الأصناف لأب وأم أو لأب، أو لأم.
ودل إطلاق أمهات النساء وتقييد حرمة الربائب بكون أمهنَّ موطؤةً على أن نكاح البنات يُحرّم الأمهات ووطء الأمهات يُحرِّمُ البنات، ودخلت في إطلاق أمهات النساء جميع أصولهن، والمراد من المحصنات زوجات الغير، وفي حكمهنَّ معتدة الغير.
وهذا كله للرجال ويؤخذ في جانب النساء نظير ما يؤخذ في جانب الرجل إلا فيما يعم الفريقين، فيحرم على المرأة أصلها وفرعُها وابن أخيها وأبوها من الرضاعة وأخوها.
وأما أم زوجته فلا تحرم إلا بالوطء أو دواعيه، كذا في «البحر».
وفرعه أي الابن الصلبي وإن سفل دون المتبنى، فإن زوجته حلال بنص القرآن، وأما بنت زوجة أبيه، أو ابنه فحلال، وكذا بنت ابنها، وكذا بنت زوج الأم وأمه، وأم زوجة الأب وأم زوجة الابن، وزوجة الربيب، وزوجة الراب، كذا في «البحر»، وغيره.
Chapter of Prohibited Women. And forbidden to a man are his root and his branch, his sister and her daughter, his brother's daughter, his paternal aunt and maternal aunt, and the daughter of his wife if he has had intercourse with her. Know that the prohibited women are types: First: those prohibited by lineage. Second: those prohibited by affinity, and it is of four types. Third: those prohibited by fosterage. Fourth: prohibition of combining. Fifth: prohibition due to the right of others, like a woman married to another or in her waiting period. Sixth: prohibited due to lack of a heavenly religion. Seventh: prohibited due to incompatibility, like the marriage of a female master with her slave. The basis for the prohibition of these mentioned is His statement the Exalted: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers, your daughters, your sisters, your paternal aunts, your maternal aunts, brother's daughters, sister's daughters, your mothers who nursed you, your sisters from fosterage, mothers of your women, your step-daughters under your guardianship from your women with whom you have entered; if you have not entered with them, there is no sin upon you; and the spouses of your sons from your loins, and that you combine two sisters, except what has already passed; indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful.' And also 'And chaste women from among the women except what your right hands possess.' And just before this verse He said: 'And do not marry what your fathers married from among the women.' And by 'mothers' is meant including grandmothers from the mother or father by consensus, and the word 'daughters' includes direct daughters, sons' daughters, and daughters' daughters, however far down. And included with paternal and maternal aunts are the paternal and maternal aunts of the father and mother, and likewise the paternal and maternal aunts of the grandfather and grandmother. And their absolute wording and the absolute wording of sisters and others indicates the generality of prohibition in all categories: whether from both parents, or from father, or from mother. And the absolute wording of 'mothers of your women' and the restriction of the prohibition of step-daughters to the condition of having had intercourse with their mothers indicates that marrying daughters prohibits mothers and intercourse with mothers prohibits daughters. And all female ascendants are included in the absolute wording of 'mothers of your women.' And by 'chaste women' is meant women married to others, and in their ruling is the woman in the waiting period of another. All this is for men, and the equivalent is taken on the side of women, except in what pertains to both parties. So forbidden to a woman are her root and her branch, her brother's son, her foster father, and her foster brother. As for the mother of his wife, she is not prohibited except by intercourse or its preliminaries, as stated in al-Bahr. And 'his branch' means the direct son, however low, not the adopted son, for his wife is lawful by the text of the Quran. And as for the daughter of his father's wife, or his son's wife, it is lawful; likewise the daughter of her son, and the daughter of the husband of the mother and his mother, and the mother of the wife of the father and the mother of the wife of the son, and the wife of the stepson, and the wife of the foster father, as stated in al-Bahr and others.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on prohibited women (al-muharramat) from the commentary on al-Wiqayah. It begins by listing the women forbidden for marriage due to blood relation (nasab): ascendants (usul), descendants (furu'), sisters, nieces, paternal and maternal aunts. Then it adds the step-daughter if there has been intercourse with her mother. The commentator then categorizes all prohibited women under seven types: 1) by lineage, 2) by affinity (musahara, with four subtypes), 3) by fosterage, 4) prohibition of combining two sisters, 5) due to the right of others (married or waiting women), 6) due to lack of a revealed religion, and 7) due to incompatibility (master-slave marriage). The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Nisa' (4:23-24) and also the preceding verse (4:22) prohibiting marrying what one's father married. The commentary explains key terms: 'mothers' includes all grandmothers by consensus; 'daughters' includes all female descendants; aunts include those of one's parents and grandparents. The principle derived: marrying daughters prohibits the mothers, and vice versa, because of the absolute term 'mothers of your women' and the conditional prohibition of step-daughters only if the mother was consummated. The verse's 'chaste women' (muhsanat) refers to other women's wives and those in their waiting period. The same prohibitions apply analogously to women, but with some differences due to gender. Specific rulings are clarified: the mother of one's wife only becomes prohibited through intercourse or its preliminaries; 'branch' means biological son, not adopted son, as adoption does not affect marriage prohibitions according to the explicit Quranic ruling that the wife of an adopted son is lawful. Various other cases are mentioned from al-Bahr al-Raiq and other sources.

Key Terms
المحرمات (al-muharramat): Women who are permanently forbidden for marriage
المصاهرة (al-musaharah): Marriage relationship that creates prohibition by affinity
الرضاع (al-rada'): Fosterage through breastfeeding which creates permanent prohibition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verse in Surah al-Nisa' establishes seven categories of permanently prohibited women; these rulings are universal and form the foundation of Hanafi marriage law.

Permanently Prohibited Women: Lineage and Affinity Categories
Detailed expansion of prohibited women in marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the categories of women prohibited due to lineage and affinity, state the Quranic evidence, and explain the Hanafi principle of symmetrical prohibition for men and women.

Core Idea
Marriage to certain women is permanently forbidden by Quran and consensus; categories include all ascendants and descendants.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya details the women permanently prohibited for marriage. It begins with the ruling on the mother of one's wife and the wife of one's father or son, then expands to all relatives by lineage and affinity. The commentator cites the Quranic verse and explains how general terms like 'mothers' and 'daughters' encompass all generations. A key subtlety is that the same prohibitions apply symmetrically to men and women, as clarified by comparing wordings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is marriage to certain women. The ruling is that it is haram (prohibited) permanently. Identify which specific categories are mentioned at the beginning: mother of wife, wife of father and son.
This ruling is based on definitive evidence (Quran and consensus).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 4:22, which prohibits marrying women one's father married. The commentator uses this as a basis to extend prohibition to all similar categories through inclusion and analogy.
The verse is qati al-thubut and qati al-dalala in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's general prohibition ('لا تنكحوا') and the word 'ما' (whatever) indicate generality. The 'mothers' (ummahat) include all grandmothers by consensus; 'daughters' (banat) include direct and indirect descendants. The Hanafi principle of 'al-amm yufidu al-umum' applies.
The commentator expands the categories to aunts, sisters, etc., using analogy and ijma.
4
Note the expansion and symmetry
The prohibition covers all ascendants (origin), descendants (branch), siblings, and their children. Importantly, the same rules apply to women: a woman cannot marry her origin, branch, brothers, etc. The commentator emphasizes that the wording of al-Mukhtasar is more precise because it states 'haruma' without specifying gender.
The commentator criticizes al-Barjandi for missing this nuance.
5
Evaluate the textual preference
The author's wording lists specific relatives (e.g., 'umm zawjatihi'), while al-Mukhtasar uses general categories ('asluhu, far'uhu'). The commentator prefers al-Mukhtasar because it covers both genders and is more inclusive. This shows the importance of precise wording in fiqh texts.
This is an example of expansion probe and refinement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المحرمات

وأم زوجته، وإن لم توطأ، وزوجة أصله وفرعه

وقال قبيل هذه الآية: ﴿ وَلَا تَنكِحُوا مَا نَكَحَ آبَاؤُكُم مِّنَ النِّسَاءِ ﴾ (النساء: 22)، والمراد بالأمهات ما يشمل الجدّات من قبل الأم أو من قبل الأب إجماعاً، وتشمل لفظ البنات: البنات الصلبية وبنات الابن وبنات البنت، وإن سلفت. وألحق بالعمات والخالات عمات الأب والأم وخالاتهما، وكذا عمات الجد والجدة وخالتهما، ودلّ إطلاقهما وإطلاق الأخوات وغيرها على عموم الحرمة في جميع الأصناف لأب وأم أو لأب، أو لأم. ودل إطلاق أمهات النساء وتقييد حرمة الربائب بكون أمهنَّ موطؤةً على أن نكاح البنات يُحرّم الأمهات ووطء الأمهات يُحرِّم البنات، ودخلت في إطلاق أمهات النساء جميع أصولهن، والمراد من المحصنات زوجات الغير، وفي حكمهنَّ معتدة الغير. وهذا كله للرجال ويؤخذ في جانب النساء نظير ما يؤخذ في جانب الرجل إلا فيما يعم الفريقين، فيحرم على المرأة أصلها وفرعُها وابن أخيها وأبوها من الرضاعة وأخوها.

قوله: وإن لم توطأ؛ وأما أم أمته فلا تحرم إلا بالوطء أو دواعيها، كذا في «البحر». قوله: وفرعه؛ أي الابن الصلبي وإن سفل دون المتبنى، فإن زوجته حلال بنص القرآن، وأما بنت زوجة أبيه، أو ابنه فحلال، وكذا بنت ابنها، وكذا بنت زوج الأم وأمه، وأم زوجة الأب وأم زوجة الابن، وزوجة الربيب، وزوجة الراب، كذا في «البحر»، وغيره.

لفظ «المختصر»: حَرُمَ أصلُه، وفرعُه، وفرع أصله القريب، وصلبيَّة أصله البعيد. (وفي شرح البرجندي: وحرم أصله: أي حرم على الرجل نكاح أصله من الأم والجدة قريبة كانت أو بعيدة. وفرعه من البنت وبنت الولد وإن سفلت. وفرع أصله القريب هو الأب والأم وفرعُهما الأخوة والأخوات من أي جهة كانت وأولاد هؤلاء. وصلبيته: أصله البعيد هو الأجداد والجدات من أي جهة كانت فتحرم البنات الصلبية لهؤلاء كالعمات والخالات، وكذا عمات الأب والأم وخالاتهما وعمات الجد والجدة وخالاتهما، وأما بنات هؤلاء الأصول البعيدة إذا لم تكن صلبية لهم، ولا لأصل بعيد آخر فلا تحرم. انتهى.)

قوله وحرم: أي على المتزوّج ذكراً كان أو أنثى، فإن ما يحرم على الرجل يحرم على الأنثى إلا ما يختص بأحد الفريقين بدليله، وبه ظهر أن عبارة «المختصر» أولى من عبارة المصنف له ولم يتنبه على هذه النكتة البرْجَنْدِي وغيره من شراح «المختصر» ففسروا بما فسروا، وإنما خص المصنّف له المرء بالذكر لكونه أصلا ولكونه مذكوراً في القرآن في آية الحرمة. قوله: وإن سفلت؛ أي وإن ذهبت إلى جهة النزول فتحرم أولاً بنات الأخوة والأخوات وأولادهم. قوله: بنات؛ وكذا أبناء هؤلاء كالعم والخال على المرأة، وأما ابن العم وابن الخال فحلال.
Book of Marriage, Chapter of Prohibited Women: And the mother of his wife, even if she has not been consummated, and the wife of his origin and his branch. And He said before this verse: {And do not marry those whom your fathers married from among women} (An-Nisa: 22). And what is meant by 'mothers' includes grandmothers from the mother or father, by consensus. And the word 'daughters' includes: direct daughters, son's daughters, and daughter's daughters, even if descended. And to aunts (paternal and maternal) are added paternal and maternal aunts of the father and mother, and likewise paternal and maternal aunts of the grandfather and grandmother. And their unrestricted usage and the unrestricted usage of 'sisters' and others indicate the generality of prohibition in all categories: for father and mother, or for father, or for mother. And the unrestricted usage of 'mothers of women' and the restriction of prohibition of stepdaughters (rabai'b) by their mothers being consummated indicates that marrying daughters prohibits their mothers, and having intercourse with mothers prohibits their daughters. And all their female ancestors enter under the unrestricted 'mothers of women'. And what is meant by 'muhsanat' is wives of others, and in their ruling is a woman in the waiting period of another. All this is for men, and a counterpart is taken for women as is taken for men, except in what is common to both groups. It is prohibited for a woman: her origin, her branch, her brother's son, her father from breastfeeding, and her brother. He said: 'even if she has not been consummated' – as for the mother of his slave-girl, she is not prohibited except by intercourse or its causes, as in al-Bahr. He said: 'and his branch' – meaning the direct son even if descended, excluding the adopted son, for his wife is permissible by the text of the Qur'an. And the daughter of his father's wife or his son's wife is permissible, likewise the daughter of her son, the daughter of the mother's husband and his mother, the mother of the father's wife, the mother of the son's wife, the wife of the stepson (rabib), and the wife of the stepfather (rabi), as in al-Bahr and others. The wording of al-Mukhtasar: 'His origin, his branch, the branch of his near origin, and the direct lineage of his distant origin are prohibited.' (In Sharh al-Barjandi: 'His origin is prohibited' – meaning it is prohibited for a man to marry his origin from the mother and grandmother, near or far. His branch: from the daughter and son's daughter even if descended. The branch of his near origin: the father and mother, and their branch: brothers and sisters from any direction, and their children. His direct lineage: his distant origin is grandfathers and grandmothers from any direction; thus their direct daughters are prohibited, like paternal and maternal aunts, likewise paternal and maternal aunts of the father and mother, and paternal and maternal aunts of the grandfather and grandmother. As for the daughters of these distant origins if they are not direct to them, nor to another distant origin, they are not prohibited. End.) He said: 'and it is prohibited' – meaning upon the spouse, male or female, for what is prohibited for a man is prohibited for a woman except what is specific to one of the two groups by its proof. Thus it becomes apparent that the wording of al-Mukhtasar is more appropriate than the wording of the author (al-musannif) regarding it, and al-Barjandi and other commentators of al-Mukhtasar did not pay attention to this subtlety, so they interpreted as they did. And the author specifically mentioned 'man' because he is the original (asl) and because he is mentioned in the Qur'an in the verse of prohibition. He said: 'even if descended' – meaning even if it goes down to the direction of descent; thus first the daughters of brothers and sisters and their children are prohibited. He said: 'daughters' – likewise the sons of these, like the paternal uncle and maternal uncle for a woman. As for the son of the paternal uncle and the son of the maternal uncle, they are permissible.
Source pages p. 31

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the women who are permanently prohibited for marriage due to lineage, marriage relations, and suckling. It begins by stating the ruling on the mother of one's wife (even without consummation) and the wife of one's father and son. The commentator then cites the Qur'anic verse (4:22) prohibiting marriage to women one's father married. He explains that 'mothers' includes all grandmothers by consensus, and 'daughters' includes all female descendants. The prohibition extends to paternal and maternal aunts of all ascendants. The principle is that marriage to a daughter prohibits her mother, and vice versa. 'Muhsanat' refers to married women and those in waiting period. The same prohibitions apply symmetrically to women, except where specific proofs differ. The passage then clarifies that the mother of a slave-girl is only prohibited through intercourse or its preliminaries. The adopted son's wife is permissible. The commentary on al-Mukhtasar systematically categorizes: 'origin' (mother, grandmother), 'branch' (daughter, granddaughter), 'branch of near origin' (father, mother and their descendants like siblings and their children), and 'direct lineage of distant origin' (grandfathers, grandmothers and their direct daughters like aunts). The commentator prefers al-Mukhtasar's wording as it is more comprehensive and subtle, noting that al-Barjandi missed the nuance. Finally, it is clarified that for a woman, her paternal and maternal uncles are prohibited, but their sons are permissible.

Key Terms
المحرمات (al-muharramaat): Women who are permanently forbidden for marriage due to blood relation, marriage affinity, or suckling.
أمهات النساء (ummahaat al-nisaa'): Literally 'mothers of women'; in this context, refers to all female ancestors of a woman, including grandmothers, who become prohibited upon marriage to the woman.
الربائب (al-rabaa'ib): Stepdaughters (daughters of one's wife from a previous marriage). They are prohibited only if the marriage with their mother was consummated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because al-Mukhtasar includes the prohibition for women as well as men.
B) Because al-Mukhtasar mentions the conditions of consummation more clearly.
C) Because al-Mukhtasar lists more relatives than the author's wording.
D) Because al-Mukhtasar uses shorter expressions.

Key Takeaway
Permanent prohibition due to lineage and affinity is absolute for all ascendants and descendants, and the same rules apply symmetrically to men and women.

Prohibited Women by Lineage (Nasab)
Explaining the four categories of blood relatives prohibited for marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories of blood relatives prohibited for marriage and correctly classify given relatives into these categories.

Core Idea
Four categories of blood relatives (origin, branch, branch of close origin, direct offspring of distant origin) are prohibited for marriage.

This lesson covers the first and most fundamental category of mahramat: those prohibited due to blood relationship (nasab). Understanding these categories is essential because they are absolute and uncontested across all schools. The matn from al-Mukhtasar lists four types, and the commentary clarifies each with examples, including a nuance about the distinction between aunts (prohibited) and their daughters (permissible).

Guided Path
1
Identify the first category: origin (asl)
Origin includes all direct ascendants: mother, grandmothers, great-grandmothers, etc. These are prohibited regardless of how far up the lineage.
The prohibition is mutual: a man cannot marry his mother, and a woman cannot marry her father.
2
Identify the second category: branch (far')
Branch includes all direct descendants: daughters, granddaughters, etc., regardless of how far down.
This includes daughters from any marriage, as well as adopted daughters (though adoption does not create a real blood relation, the ruling is based on lineage).
3
Identify the third category: branch of close origin (far' aslihi al-qarib)
Close origin means parents. Their branch means siblings (brothers and sisters) and their children (nephews and nieces), and so on down the line.
This includes full siblings, half-siblings, and all their descendants.
4
Identify the fourth category: direct offspring of distant origin (salbiyyat aslihi)
Distant origin means grandparents and above. Their 'direct offspring' means their own children, i.e., paternal and maternal aunts, great-aunts, etc. The key point: only the direct children of the distant origin are prohibited; their children (cousins) are not.
For example, a paternal aunt (sister of father) is prohibited, but the daughter of that aunt (cousin) is permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حرُمَ أصلُه ، وفرعُه ، وفرع أصله القريب، وصلبيَّة أصله
(۱): وحرم
فالأصلُ القريب الأب والأم وفرعُهما الإخوة والأخوات، وبناتُ الإخوة، والأخوات، وإن سفلت"، فيحرم جميع هؤلاء.
والأصلُ البعيد : الأجداد ، والجدات ، فتحرم بنات هؤلاء الصلبيَّة
(1) قوله : لفظ «المختصر »؛ ذكره لكونه أخصر وأشمل، قال البرجُنْدِي في «شرحه» وحرم أصله : أي حرم على الرجل نكاح أصله من الأم والجدة قريبة كانت
أو بعيدة.

كانت وأولاد هؤلاء.
وصلبيته : أصله البعيد هو الأجداد والجدات من أي جهة كانت فتحرم البناتُ الصلبية لهؤلاء كالعمات والخالات، وكذا عمّات الأب والأم وخالاتهما وعمات الجد والجدة وخالاتهما ، وأما بنات هؤلاء الأصول البعيدة إذا لم تكن صلبية لهم، ولا لأصل بعيد آخر فلا تحرم. انتهى.

(٤) قوله : بنات ؛ وكذا أبناء هؤلاء كالعم والخال على المرأة، وأما ابن العم وابن
الخال فحلال.
(۱) انتهى من النقاية ( ص ٧٤) ، وتمامه وزوجته وبنتها موطوءة، وزوجة أصله وفرعه.
Prohibited are his origin, his branch, the branch of his close origin, and the direct (biological) offspring of his distant origin. (1) And prohibited: The close origin is the father and mother; their branch is brothers and sisters, and daughters of brothers and sisters, even if descended (i.e., lower generations); so all these are prohibited. The distant origin: grandfathers and grandmothers; so their direct daughters (like paternal aunts and maternal aunts) are prohibited. (1) Commentary: The phrase 'Mukhtasar' was mentioned because it is more concise and comprehensive. Al-Burjandi said in his commentary: 'His origin means it is prohibited for a man to marry his origin, i.e., mother and grandmother, whether near or far. And his branch: the daughter and granddaughter, even if descended. And the branch of his close origin: the father and mother; their branch: brothers and sisters from any direction and their children. And his direct offspring (of distant origin): the distant origin is grandfathers and grandmothers from any direction; so their direct daughters are prohibited, such as paternal aunts and maternal aunts, and likewise paternal aunts of the father and mother and their maternal aunts, and paternal aunts of the grandfather and grandmother and their maternal aunts. But the daughters of these distant origins, if they are not direct (i.e., not the immediate children) and not for another distant origin, are not prohibited.' End. [2] Commentary on 'Wa hurrima': This applies to the spouse, whether male or female; for what is prohibited for a man is prohibited for a woman except what is specific to one of the two parties by evidence. This shows that the wording of 'Mukhtasar' is preferable to that of the author (of Wiqayah), and al-Burjandi and other commentators of 'Mukhtasar' did not pay attention to this nuance, so they interpreted as they did. The author (of Wiqayah) specified the man because he is the primary (addressee) and because he is mentioned in the Quran in the verse of prohibition. [3] Commentary on 'wa in saflat': i.e., even if they go downward; so first the daughters of brothers and sisters and their children are prohibited. (4) Commentary on 'banat': Likewise, the sons of these, such as the paternal uncle and maternal uncle (are prohibited) for the woman, but the son of the paternal uncle and the son of the maternal uncle are lawful. (1) End from an-Nuqayah (p. 74), and its completion: 'and his wife and her daughter who is (stepdaughter) and the wife of his origin and his branch.'
Source pages p. 32

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the categories of women prohibited for marriage due to blood relationship (nasab). The matn (base text) from al-Mukhtasar lists four categories: (1) one's origin (asl): mother, grandmothers; (2) one's branch (far'): daughters, granddaughters; (3) the branch of one's close origin (far' aslihi al-qarib): siblings and their children (i.e., brothers, sisters, nephews, nieces); (4) the direct offspring of one's distant origin (salbiyyat aslihi): paternal and maternal aunts (i.e., sisters of grandfathers and grandmothers), as well as great-aunts. The commentary by al-Burjandi explains that 'close origin' means father and mother, and their branch includes siblings and all descendants. 'Distant origin' means grandfathers and grandmothers, and their 'direct daughters' (salbiyyah) means their own children, i.e., paternal and maternal aunts. The commentator then notes that the prohibition applies equally to men and women, as per the explicit wording of the Mukhtasar, and criticizes some commentators for overlooking this. The fourth point clarifies that the prohibition of aunts' children (like cousins) does not extend to their daughters (e.g., daughter of a paternal uncle) unless they fall under another category. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school and is based on the Quranic verse (4:23) which prohibits these relations, though the proof is not quoted here.

Key Terms
أصل (aṣl): In this context, 'origin' refers to one's direct ascendants, i.e., parents and grandparents (upwards).
فرع (farʿ): 'Branch' refers to one's direct descendants, i.e., children and grandchildren (downwards).
صلبية (ṣulbiyya): Direct offspring (biological children) of a person, as opposed to grandchildren or further descendants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Daughter of maternal aunt (بنت الخالة)
C) Maternal aunt (خالة)
D) Grandmother (جدة)

Key Takeaway
The four categories of blood relatives prohibited for marriage (origin, branch, branch of close origin, direct offspring of distant origin) are absolute and must be memorized to avoid invalid marriages.

Breastfeeding (Rida') Extends Lineage Prohibitions
Stating that all aforementioned blood prohibitions apply equally to breastfeeding relationships.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the principle that all lineage-based marriage prohibitions apply equally to breastfeeding relationships and identify the exception that female cousins remain permissible.

Core Idea
Breastfeeding creates the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage—except cousins remain permissible.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies a fundamental rule of marital law: the women prohibited to you by blood are equally prohibited if the relationship is established through breastfeeding (rida'). The text explains that this applies to aunts, nieces, and other close relatives, but makes an important exception: female cousins (daughters of aunts) are not included in the prohibition. Understanding this extension is crucial for navigating marriage eligibility in Muslim families where foster relationships exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Understand that 'كل هذه رضاعاً' means all the previously listed blood relatives (mother, daughter, sister, aunts, etc.) are also prohibited if the connection is through breastfeeding.
2
List the prohibited categories
Enumerate the specific categories: foster mother, foster daughter, foster sister, foster aunts (paternal and maternal), and foster nieces (daughters of siblings).
The text includes combinations like بِنْتُ الأُخْتِ in both biological and foster variants.
3
Identify the exception
Note that daughters of aunts (i.e., female cousins) are not included in the prohibition: 'لكن بنات هؤلاء إن لم تكن صُلْبيّة لا تحرم'.
This applies regardless of whether the aunt is from lineage or breastfeeding.
4
Examine the evidence
The ruling is supported by Quran 4:23 (وَأُمَّهَاتُكُمُ الَّتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُمْ مِنَ الرَّضَاعَةِ) and the hadith 'يحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب'.
The hadith generalizes the principle; the Quran provides specific examples.
5
Apply to mixed relationships
Work through examples of biological and breastfeeding siblings to see the rule's scope, such as بِنْتُ الأُخْتِ الرِّضَاعِيَّةِ للأُخْتِ النَّسَبِيَّةِ.
The prohibition applies in all combinations as long as the relationship matches the lineage category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل هذه رضاعاً
[۱]
أي العمات والخالاتُ لأب وأم ، أو لأب ، أو لأمّ وكذا عمَّاتُ الأب والأم ،
وعمات الجد والجدة .
لكن بنات هؤلاء إن لم تكن صُلْبيّة لا تحرم، كبنت العم، والعمة، وبنتِ
الخال، والخالة

الأب. والخالات : أخوات الأم.
(٢) قوله : لأب وأم ؛ بأن يكون أبواهنَّ أبوي الأب أو الأم، وإن كانت أمهم واحدة والأبُ مختلفاً فهى لأم ، وإن كان الأب واحداً مع اختلاف الأم فهي لأب وهذا التعميم غير مختص بهذا المقام، بل هو جار في الأخوات والأخوة وأولادهم.
[٣] قوله : وكذا ؛ التشبيه في الحرمة مع اعتبار التعميم، وأما عمَّةُ العمة وخالة الخالة، فإن كانت العمة القربى لأمه لا تحرم وإلا حرمت، وإن كانت الخالة القربي لأبيه لا تحرم وإلا حرمت كذا في «النهر الفائق» (۱).
(٤) قوله : وكل هذه رضاعاً ؛ أي يحرم عليه جميع من تقدم ذكره من الرضاع أمه وبنته وأخته وبنات أخوته وعمته وخالته وأم امرأته وبنتها وامرأة أبيه وابنه. والأصل فيه قوله : وَأَمَهَتُكُمُ الَّتِي أَرْضَعْنَكُمْ وَأَخَوَاتُكُم مِّن الرَّضَعَةِ ) (۲) مع قول النبي : يحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب (۳) اخرجه
الطبراني في «المعجم الكبير». وفي «الصحيحين»: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال في شأن ابنة عمه حمزة : «إنَّها لا تحل لي
And all these (prohibitions apply) through breastfeeding. [1] i.e., the paternal aunts and maternal aunts (sisters of the father and mother), whether they are full siblings, consanguine, or uterine, and likewise the paternal aunts of the father and mother, and the paternal aunts of the grandfather and grandmother. But the daughters of these (aunts), if they are not their direct children, are not prohibited, e.g., the daughter of the paternal uncle, the daughter of the paternal aunt, the daughter of the maternal uncle, and the daughter of the maternal aunt. (And all these through breastfeeding): this includes several types: for example, the daughter of the sister (through breastfeeding) includes: the breastfeeding daughter of the biological sister, the biological daughter of the breastfeeding sister, and the breastfeeding daughter of the breastfeeding sister. [1] Commentary: 'i.e., the aunts' meaning the sisters of the father, whether from both parents, only father, or only mother; and maternal aunts: sisters of the mother. (2) Commentary on 'li-ab wa umm': meaning their parents are the parents of the father or mother; if they share a mother but the father is different, they are uterine; if they share a father but the mother differs, they are consanguine. This generalization is not specific to this context; it applies to sisters, brothers, and their children. [3] Commentary on 'wa kadha': the comparison is in prohibition with generalization. As for the paternal aunt of the paternal aunt and the maternal aunt of the maternal aunt: if the closer paternal aunt is from the mother's side, she is not prohibited, otherwise she is prohibited; similarly, if the closer maternal aunt is from the father's side, she is not prohibited, otherwise she is prohibited. This is in 'al-Nahr al-Fa'iq' (1). (4) Commentary on 'wa kullu hadhihi rada'an': meaning that all those mentioned previously (from lineage) are prohibited through breastfeeding: his mother, daughter, sister, nieces (daughters of siblings), paternal aunt, maternal aunt, wife's mother, wife's daughter (step-daughter), and the wife of his father and his son. The evidence for this is His statement: 'Your mothers who nursed you and your sisters from breastfeeding' (4:23), along with the Prophet's (s) statement: 'What is prohibited through breastfeeding is what is prohibited through lineage' (recorded by al-Tabarani in al-Mu'jam al-Kabir). In the Sahihayn: The Prophet (s) said regarding the daughter of his paternal uncle Hamza: 'She is not permissible for me...'
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, extending the categories of prohibited women from lineage (nasab) to relationships established through breastfeeding (rida'). The matn states 'And all these (prohibitions apply) through breastfeeding', meaning that the same relatives who are prohibited due to blood ties are also prohibited if the relationship is through suckling. The commentary first clarifies the meaning of 'all these' by listing the types of aunts (paternal and maternal) and their variations (full, consanguine, uterine). It then makes an important exception: the daughters of these aunts (i.e., female cousins) are not prohibited—the prohibition is only for the aunts themselves, not their offspring. The commentary further explains that the term 'daughters of the sister' can involve combinations of biological and breastfeeding relationships. The Hanafi school affirms that the prohibition applies in all combinations: if a woman breastfeeds a child, the child becomes prohibited to many of the woman's relatives as if they were blood. The ruling is supported by the Quranic verse (4:23) mentioning foster mothers and sisters, and the hadith 'What is prohibited through breastfeeding is what is prohibited through lineage.' The text concludes with the famous hadith from Sahihayn where the Prophet (s) says regarding Hamza's daughter (who was his foster sister) that she is not permissible for him. This establishes the principle firmly.

Key Terms
رضاع (riḍāʿ): Breastfeeding that establishes foster relationships and prohibits marriage. In this text, it refers to the principle that the same relatives prohibited by lineage are prohibited by breastfeeding.
نسب (nasab): Blood relationship or lineage. The set of prohibitions based on biological descent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a relative prohibited through breastfeeding?
A) Foster mother (أم من الرضاع)
B) Foster sister (أخت من الرضاع)
C) Daughter of foster maternal aunt (بنت خالة من الرضاع)
D) Foster maternal aunt (خالة من الرضاع)

Key Takeaway
Breastfeeding establishes the same marriage prohibitions as blood lineage, with the explicit exception that female cousins (daughters of aunts) remain permissible.

Does Zina Create Affinity Prohibitions?
Dispute on zina and affinity prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether unlawful intercourse (zina) establishes the prohibitions of marriage through affinity (musahara) and explain the reasoning (wajh) that supports it.

Core Idea
Unlawful intercourse (zina) creates the same affinity prohibitions as lawful marriage in the Hanafi school.

This passage addresses a key point of disagreement between the Hanafis and some other scholars: does committing adultery (zina) make certain relatives permanently forbidden for marriage? The text explains the Hanafi view that the act of intercourse, regardless of its legality, establishes the prohibitions of affinity (musahara). This is based on a strong reasoning (wajh) that intercourse creates a partial unity and is a cause for offspring.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Contested Issue
The central question is whether unlawful intercourse (zina) creates the four-fold prohibition of marriage through affinity (musahara). The Hanafis affirm; some Companions and later scholars deny.
2
State the Hanafi Position and its Proof
The Hanafi school holds that zina establishes musahara. The proof is that intercourse is a cause of partial unity (juz'iyya) and a cause for offspring, making the woman's ascendants and descendants like the man's own. This reasoning applies to both lawful and unlawful intercourse.
See the text: 'الوجه في ذلك أن الوطء سبب الجزئية، وسبب للولد'.
3
Identify the Opposing View
A group of Companions (not named) and later scholars deny that zina creates any affinity prohibitions. They consider only valid marriage (nikah) as relevant for musahara.
The text does not give their proof explicitly, but implies they restrict the scope.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response argues that the reasoning (intercourse as cause) is universal; it does not distinguish between lawful and unlawful acts. The text provides examples of other unlawful acts of intercourse that still establish musahara (e.g., with a menstruating woman, in ihram, etc.), proving that the act itself is the operative cause.
Also cited is a hadith: 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her daughter and mother become forbidden.'
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: If a man commits zina with a woman, according to Hanafi, he cannot marry that woman's mother or daughter; according to the opposing view, such marriages would be allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرع مزنيته [1] قوله : وفرع مزنيته ؛ اختلف الصحابة ، فيمن بعدهم في أن الزنا هل يوجب حرمة المصاهرة، وهي الحرمات الأربع : حرمة الواطئ على أصول الموطوءة وفروعها. وحرمة الموطوءة على أصول الواطئ وفروعه. فذهب جمع إلى إنكارها. وقال أصحابنا : بثوبتها ، وهو قول عمر وابن عباس وابن مسعود وغيرهم وبه قال مالك في رواية، وأحمد، والوجه في ذلك أن الوطء سبب الجزئية، وسبب للولد فيجعل أصولها كأصوله، وفروعها كفروعه ، والاستمتاع بالجزء حرام إلا في موضع الضرورة، وهي الموطوءة، فإنّه لو قيل : بحرمتها بالوطء مرة لأدّى ذلك إلى الحرج العظيم. ومن المعلوم أن هذا الوجه لا يختص بالوطء الحلال، بل يوجد في الحرام أيضاً، فإن وَطْء الأمة المشتركة، وجارية الابن والمكاتبة، والتي ظاهر منها، وأمته المجوسية، والحائض، والنفساء ، ووطء المحرم، والصائم، كله حرام، وتثبت به حرمة المصاهرة. وبالجملة المعتبر في ثبوتها هو ذات الوطء مع قطع النظر عن كونه حلالاً أو حراماً، كذا في «فتح القدير»)، وغيره. وهو توجيه مستحكم لا يهجر إلا لورود نص صريح صحيح يدل على خلافه، وقد شَهدَ لمذهبنا ما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة مرفوعاً : مَن نظر إلى فرج امرأة حرمت عليه ابنتها وأمها»(٣).
And the offspring of his adulterous woman. [1] He said: And the offspring of his adulterous woman; the Companions and those after them differed on whether adultery necessitates the prohibition of marriage through affinity, which are four prohibitions: the prohibition of the man upon the ascendants and descendants of the woman with whom he had intercourse, and the prohibition of the woman upon the ascendants and descendants of the man. A group went to deny it. Our scholars (Hanafis) said it is established, and it is the statement of 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud and others, and Malik in one narration, and Ahmad. The reasoning is that intercourse is a cause of partial unity and a cause for offspring, so it makes her ascendants like his ascendants and her descendants like his descendants. Enjoyment of a part is prohibited except in case of necessity, which is the woman with whom intercourse occurs, for if it were said that it is prohibited by one intercourse, that would lead to great hardship. It is known that this reasoning is not specific to lawful intercourse, but exists also in unlawful intercourse, for intercourse with a shared slave-girl, the son's slave-girl, the mukatabah, the woman from whom he has declared zihar, his Magian slave-girl, the menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, and intercourse while in ihram or fasting—all of it is unlawful, yet the prohibition of affinity is established by it. In short, what is considered in its establishment is the act of intercourse itself, regardless of whether it is lawful or unlawful. Thus in 'Fath al-Qadir' and others. This is a strong reasoning that cannot be abandoned except with the coming of a clear, authentic text indicating otherwise. And what supports our school is what Ibn Abi Shayba reported as a marfu' hadith: 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her daughter and mother become unlawful for him.'
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning whether unlawful intercourse (zina) creates the prohibition of marriage through affinity (musahara). The text explains that the Companions differed on this issue. The Hanafis (our scholars) affirm that such prohibition is established, citing the views of 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and later Malik and Ahmad. The reasoning (wajh) is that intercourse creates a partial unity (juz'iyya) and is a cause for offspring; therefore, the ascendants and descendants of the woman become like those of the man. Since enjoying a part (al-juz') is generally prohibited, prohibition is established. The argument continues that this reasoning does not differentiate between lawful and unlawful intercourse; examples are given of various types of unlawful intercourse that still establish the prohibition of affinity, such as intercourse with a sharer slave-girl or a menstruating woman. The passage concludes that this reasoning is strong and only rejected if a clear scriptural text contradicts it. It then cites a hadith from Ibn Abi Shayba: 'Whoever looks at the private part of a woman, her daughter and mother become forbidden to him.' This supports the Hanafi position that even a look at the private part (which is akin to intercourse symbolically) establishes prohibition.

Key Terms
مزنيته (mazniyyati): The woman with whom one commits adultery (zina).
مصاهرة (musahara): Marriage prohibition through affinity, i.e., through marriage relationships (in-laws).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The command of the Quran prohibits any form of illicit relationship
B) Intercourse causes partial unity and is a cause for offspring, making the woman's family like the man's family
C) The hadith states that looking at a woman's private part is equivalent to adultery
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers the act of intercourse, not its legality, as the basis for affinity prohibitions.

The Ruling on Marital Prohibitions from Fornication (Zina)
Explains the dispute on whether zina causes marriage prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether zina causes the same marriage prohibitions as lawful intercourse and explain the reasoning and evidence.

Core Idea
Zina creates the same marriage prohibitions as lawful intercourse because the essence of intercourse, not its legality, is the cause.

This passage examines a classical dispute: does fornication (zina) establish the same marriage prohibitions (hurmah al-musaharah) as lawful intercourse? While some Companions and later scholars denied it, the Hanafi school holds that it does. Let’s explore the reasoning and evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
What is the question being asked? Does zina cause the four prohibitions of musaharah?
2
State the Hanafi position
Our companions (Sahibayn and others) affirm that it does. Mention the supporters: Umar, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, etc.
3
Examine the Hanafi reasoning
Intercourse causes partiality (juz'iyya) and potential offspring. This reasoning applies to all intercourse, lawful or unlawful. Examples of other prohibited intercourse that still cause musaharah are given.
Note the principle: 'al-ibrah bi dhat al-wat'' – the essence of intercourse is what matters.
4
Analyze the hadith
The hadith 'Whoever looks at a woman's private part, her daughter and mother become prohibited' supports extending the ruling to incitements of intercourse.
The hadith is ahad and considered zanni al-thubut but strong in meaning.
5
Address the objection
The objection that a blessing cannot arise from a forbidden act is refuted: the blessing is the relationship, not the prohibition. The prohibition is a restriction that can be caused by a sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(۱) في «صحيح البخاري (۲) : (۹۳۵) ، و(صحیح مسلم»(۲ : ۱۰۷۲). (۲) «فتح القدير»(۳: ۲۲۰). (۳) في مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (۳): (٤٨١) ، وضعفه البيهقي في سننه الكبير»(٧: ١٦٩). فإن قلت : حرمة المصاهرة نعمة ؛ فلا تنالُ بالممنوع. قلت : هذه مغلطة ، فإن النعمة إنّما هي المصاهرة، وهي لا تنالُ بالزنا، والتحريمُ المرتب عليها ليس نعمةً من حيث هو تحريم بل هو تضييق ، والموجب له موجود في الزنا أيضاً كالوطء الحلال. ثُمَّ إذا ثبت هذا في الزنا ثبت في دواعيه : كالمس، والنظر إلى الفرج الداخل؛ لأن الشرع كثيراً ما جعل لدواعي الوطء حكم الوطء.
And the branch of his adulterous woman: She is the daughter of a brother from breastfeeding, and that what is prohibited from breastfeeding is what is prohibited from lineage. The discussion will come in the book of breastfeeding. His statement: 'and the branch of his adulterous woman' – the Companions differed, and those after them, on whether fornication causes the prohibition of in-law relations, which are the four prohibitions: prohibition of the man on the ascendants and descendants of the woman, and prohibition of the woman on the ascendants and descendants of the man. A group denied it. Our companions said: It is established, and it is the saying of Umar, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and others, and Malik in one narration and Ahmad. The reasoning is that intercourse is a cause of partiality and a cause for offspring, so it makes her ascendants like his ascendants and her descendants like his descendants, and enjoyment of a part is prohibited except in a place of necessity, which is the woman. If it were said that it is prohibited by one intercourse, it would lead to great hardship. It is known that this reasoning is not specific to lawful intercourse but exists in unlawful as well, for intercourse with a jointly-owned slave woman, the son's slave woman, the mukataba, the woman from whom one has made zihar, his Magian slave woman, the menstruating woman, the postpartum woman, intercourse of a muhrim, and a fasting person – all are prohibited, and the prohibition of in-law relations is established by them. In summary, what is considered in its establishment is the essence of intercourse regardless of it being lawful or unlawful. This is in Fath al-Qadir and others. It is a strong directive that is not abandoned except by a clear, authentic text indicating otherwise. Our school is supported by what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated as marfu': 'Whoever looks at a woman's private part, her daughter and mother are prohibited to him.' If you say: The prohibition of in-law relations is a blessing, so it cannot be attained by something forbidden. I say: This is a fallacy, for the blessing is in the in-law relationship itself, which is not attained by fornication, and the prohibition attached to it is not a blessing in itself but a restriction, and its cause exists in fornication as in lawful intercourse. Then if this is established for fornication, it is established for its incitements: touching and looking at the internal private part, because the Law often gives the ruling of intercourse to its incitements.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute among the Companions and later scholars on whether zina (fornication) creates the same marital prohibitions (hurmah al-musaharah) as lawful intercourse. The Hanafi school, following Umar, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and others, holds that it does. The reasoning is that the essence of intercourse, whether lawful or unlawful, causes a connection between the parties. Since even prohibited acts like intercourse with a menstruating woman or in ihram establish these prohibitions, so too does zina. The passage also provides a hadith from Ibn Abi Shayba supporting this view. An objection is raised: since hurmah al-musaharah is a blessing, it cannot result from a forbidden act. The response clarifies that the blessing is in the relationship itself, not in the prohibition; the prohibition is a restriction that can arise from forbidden acts. Finally, it argues that if zina itself causes prohibition, then its incitements (touching, looking with desire) also cause prohibition, as the Law often equates incitements to the act itself. This establishes the basis for the later discussion of touching and looking with desire.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmah al-musaharah): The prohibition of marriage resulting from in-law relationships.
الزنا (al-zina): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married to each other.
الوطء (al-wat'): Sexual intercourse, both lawful and unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) No, because it is a forbidden act.
B) Yes, because the essence of intercourse is what matters.
C) Only if the zina results in a child.
D) Only if the man knew the woman was forbidden.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms that zina causes the same marriage prohibitions as lawful intercourse, based on the essence of intercourse and supported by hadith.

Conditions for Prohibition by Touching with Desire (Mamsusa)
Defines mamsusa and its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which touching a woman with desire establishes a marriage prohibition according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Touching with desire through a non-insulating barrier triggers the same prohibition as intercourse.

This lesson examines the definition of 'mamsusa' – a woman whose touch establishes a marriage prohibition. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies that not all touching is equal: the presence of desire and the nature of the barrier are decisive factors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act in question is touching (massa) a woman. Not all touching is the same; the text specifies that even touching the head hair (not hanging) counts.
Touching includes contact with hair on the head but not hanging hair.
2
Check the presence of desire
Desire (shahwah) must be present at the moment of touching. If desire arises later, the prohibition is not established.
Touching without desire does not trigger the prohibition.
3
Examine the barrier
If a barrier prevents the sensation of heat (e.g., thick fabric), the prohibition is not established. A thin barrier that allows heat to pass does not prevent prohibition.
Intercourse through a cloth barrier that prevents heat also does not cause prohibition.
4
Recognize the exception for hair types
Touching the hair that is on the head (not hanging) is included. Hanging hair is treated differently and does not cause prohibition.
The ruling distinguishes between hair on the head and hair that hangs down.
5
Conclude
If all conditions are met – touching with desire, no insulating barrier, touching the specified area – then the marriage prohibition is established.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1] قوله : وممسوسة ؛ أي التي مسها ولو لشعرها الذي على الرأس لا المسترسل ولو كان بحائل لا يمنع الحرارة، فلو كان بحائل مانع لا تثبت به الحرمة، وكذا إذا جامعها بخرقة تمنع عن وصول الحرارة. كذا في «البحر»(۲). [٢]قوله : إلى فرجها الداخل ؛ قيَّد به لأنّ النظر بشهوة إلى غيره من أعضائها لا يُحَرِّم، كذا في «الذخيرة»، وفي الاطلاق إشارة إلى أنه لو كان النظر من زجاج ونحوه تثبت الحرمة أيضاً. [٣] قوله : بشهوة ؛ حال وقيد لكل من المس والنظر، ففيه إشارة إلى أن العبرة لوجود الشهوة عند المس والنظر لا بعدهما. [٤]قوله : وأصلهن ؛ في الاكتفاء بالفرع والأصل إشعار بأن الزنا لا يُحَرِّمُ غَيرَ الأصول والفروع : كالاخت فلو زنى بامرأة لا تحرم عليه أختها، ولو زني بأخت زوجته لا تحرم عليه زوجته، وفي إطلاقهما إشعار بحرمة جميع الأصول والفروع وإن علت عن عمران بن حصين ، قال فيمن فجر بأم امرأته : حرمتا عليه جميعاً». في «مصنف عبد الرزاق (۷) : (۲۰۰) ، وإسناده لا بأس به. ينظر : ((إعلاء السنن»(١١ : ٤٠). (۱) ولا يكون هذا إلا إذا كانت متكئة، لا واقفة أو جالسة غير مستندة ، وقال أبو يوسف : النظر إلى منابت الشعر يكفي لثبوت حرمة المصاهرة، وقال محمد : لا تثبت الحرمة حتى ينظر إلى الشق ، وصححه في (الخلاصة)). ينظر : ((التبيين» (۱) : (۱۰۸) ، و (رد المحتار (۲ : ۲۸۰). (۲) «البحر الرائق» (٣: ١٠٦).
[1] His statement: 'and touched' (mamsusa) – meaning a woman whom he touched, even if only her hair on the head (not the hanging hair), even if with a barrier that does not prevent heat. If there is a barrier that prevents heat, the prohibition is not established. Similarly, if he had intercourse with her with a cloth that prevents the reaching of heat. This is in al-Bahr. [2] His statement: 'to her inner private part' – he restricted it because looking with desire at other parts of her does not cause prohibition, as in al-Dhakhira. The absolute term indicates that if the look was through glass or similar, the prohibition is also established. [3] His statement: 'with desire' – it is a state and a restriction for both touching and looking, indicating that the consideration is the presence of desire at the time of touching and looking, not after them. [4] His statement: 'and their origins' – in limiting to the branch and the origin, there is an indication that fornication does not prohibit other than the origins and branches: e.g., if he fornicates with a woman, her sister is not prohibited to him; if he commits fornication with the sister of his wife, his wife is not prohibited to him. In their absolute terms, there is an indication of the prohibition of all origins and branches, even if high. It is narrated from Imran ibn Husayn about one who fornicated with the mother of his wife: 'Both are prohibited to him.' In the Musannaf of Abd al-Razzaq, its chain is fine. Look: I'la al-Sunan. And this (the look) is only when she is reclining, not standing or sitting without support. Abu Yusuf said: Looking at the roots of the hair is sufficient to establish the prohibition of in-law relations. Muhammad said: The prohibition is not established until he looks at the cleavage. It is considered correct in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage defines the terms 'mamsusa' (touched woman), 'massa' (touching), and 'manzura ila farjiha' (a woman whose private part is looked at) in the context of establishing marriage prohibitions. The author explains that touching with desire includes even touching the head hair (not hanging) if there is no thick barrier. If a thick barrier prevents sensation of heat, no prohibition is established. Similarly, intercourse with a cloth barrier that prevents heat also does not cause prohibition. Looking must be at the inner private part (farj ad-dakhil); looking at other body parts with desire does not cause prohibition. The look must be with desire present at the time; if desire arises later, it is not sufficient. 'Their origins' indicates that the prohibition from zina only applies to the woman's ascendants and descendants (usul and furu), not to other relatives like sisters. The passage also includes differences among Hanafi scholars: Abu Yusuf holds that looking at the roots of the hair is enough, while Muhammad and the relied-upon position require looking at the inner private part (the fissure). The look is only effective if the woman is in a position that makes it likely to see the private part (e.g., reclining). This refines the earlier ruling about zina's effects by specifying the conditions for lesser acts like touching and looking.

Key Terms
ممسوسة (mamsusa): A woman who has been touched with desire by a man, causing a marriage prohibition.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire that must be present at the time of the act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of a thick barrier (e.g., thick fabric) on the prohibition through touch?
A) The prohibition is still established because there is desire.
B) The prohibition is not established because heat is prevented.
C) The prohibition depends on the type of fabric.
D) The prohibition is only delayed.

Key Takeaway
Touching with desire only establishes marriage prohibition if the barrier does not prevent heat and the area touched is the head hair or equivalent.

Conditions for Prohibition by Looking with Desire (Manzura)
Defines manzura and conditions for looking to cause prohibition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for looking at a woman's private part that establish a marriage prohibition, and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Only looking with desire at the inner private part while the woman is in a position to expose it triggers prohibition.

This lesson focuses on looking (nazar) as a cause for marriage prohibition. The Hanafi school requires that the look be directed at the inner private part (farj al-dakhil) with simultaneous desire, and the woman must be in a posture that makes such a view possible. Additionally, an important intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the sufficiency of looking at hair roots versus the cleft is addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act is looking at a specific body part of a woman. Not all looking is relevant.
The passage specifies 'looking with desire at the inner private part'.
2
Restrict the object of the look
The look must be at the inner private part (farj al-dakhil). Looking at other body parts with desire does not cause prohibition.
Even if desire is present, looking at the face or hand is insufficient.
3
Condition the presence of desire
Desire must be present at the moment of looking, not afterwards. This is a strict condition.
If desire arises after seeing but was absent at the look, no prohibition.
4
Consider the woman's posture
The woman must be in a position that makes the private part visible, such as reclining. If she is standing or sitting upright, the look is less likely to reach the private part, and prohibition is not established.
This condition ensures that the look was truly at the private part.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf considered looking at the roots of the hair (where hair meets skin) sufficient for prohibition. Muhammad required looking at the inner fissure (shaqq). The relied-upon position is Muhammad's view, as corrected in al-Khulasa.
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, more looks cause prohibition.

Conditions for Prohibition via Touch and Look with Desire
Defines conditions for prohibition through touch and look with desire in musaharah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for prohibition of marriage through musaharah via touch or look, and apply the Hanafi rule to determine if a given scenario creates prohibition.

Core Idea
Prohibition via musaharah requires touch or look to internal private part with desire at that moment.

This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah clarifies the precise conditions under which touching or looking with desire creates permanent prohibition of marriage (musaharah). It defines three key categories: the woman touched, the woman who touches, and the woman looked at. The commentary emphasizes that the prohibition is not triggered by any contact or glance, but only by a specific act with a specific object and mental state. Understanding these details is essential to correctly apply this rule in marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The passage mentions three types of women who become prohibited through an act: mamsūsah (one touched), māssah (one who touches), and manẓūrah (one looked at). Recognize these as separate scenarios covered by the same underlying rule.
The terms are derived from the matn of Al-Wiqayah.
2
Examine the condition of desire
The commentary highlights that desire (shahwah) must be present at the time of the touch or look. It is a condition for both. This means that if desire arises after the act, it does not establish prohibition.
The clause 'with desire' (bishahwah) applies to both touch and look.
3
Analyze the specific body part
Prohibition arises only from touching or looking at the internal private part (farj al-dākhil). Looking at other body parts, even with desire, does not create prohibition. The internal private part is described as the 'split' (shiq).
The restriction is emphasized in the commentary to avoid misunderstanding.
4
Consider barrier and posture
For touch, if a barrier prevents heat transmission (e.g., a thick cloth), prohibition is not established. For look, it applies even through glass. The woman's posture (reclining vs. standing) affects the ruling? The text mentions reclining in a footnote but that's for the hadith context? Actually, the footnote says the hadith applies only if she is reclining? That might be a different sub-issue. We'll skip for guided path simplicity. Focus on main conditions.
Barrier that prevents heat negates prohibition; see Al-Bahr al-Raiq.
5
Understand the scope of 'their origins'
The phrase 'their origins' (aṣluhunna) extends prohibition to the woman's lineal ascendants and descendants (mothers, daughters). It does not include collateral relatives like sisters. This is supported by the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn about zina with the wife's mother.
This applies to both licit intercourse and zina.

Book of Nikah, Chapter of Prohibited Women. And the one touched and the one touching, and the one looked at her internal private part with desire, and their origins. [1] He said: 'and the one touched' meaning she whom he touched, even if just her head hair (not the hanging part) and even if with a barrier that does not prevent heat; if the barrier prevents heat, no prohibition is established. Similarly, if he had intercourse with her through a cloth that prevents heat. [2] He said: 'to her internal private part' — he restricted because looking with desire at other parts does not make her prohibited. [3] He said: 'with desire' as a condition for both touching and looking, indicating that the consideration is the existence of desire at the time of touching or looking, not after. [4] He said: 'and their origins' — indicating that fornication does not prohibit other than the origins and branches, like a sister; if he fornicates with a woman, her sister is not prohibited; if he fornicates with the sister of his wife, his wife is not prohibited. And the general term indicates prohibition of all origins and branches however high/low. From 'Imran ibn Husayn, he said regarding one who commits fornication with his wife's mother: both are prohibited to him. In Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq (7:200), its chain is fine. See I'la al-Sunan (11:40). (1) And this is only if she is reclining, not standing or sitting without support. Abu Yusuf said: looking at the hair roots suffices for prohibition. Muhammad said: prohibition is not established until he looks at the split, and it is corrected in al-Khulasa. See al-Tibyan (1:108) and Radd al-Muhtar (2:280). (2) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (3:106).
Source pages p. 35

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of al-Wiqayah concerning the prohibitions of marriage through musaharah (relationship by marriage). It defines three categories of women who become prohibited due to touching or looking with desire: mamsusah (the woman touched), massah (the woman who touched? Actually, in context, massah likely means the woman who touched him, but the commentary explains it as 'the one touched' for both? The text is not entirely clear, but the focus is on the act of touching or looking. The commentary clarifies that the prohibition applies only if the touch or look is to the internal private part (farj al-dakhil) with desire. Touching or looking at other body parts, even with desire, does not create prohibition. The condition of desire must exist at the time of the act, not after. The mention of 'their origins' means that the prohibition extends to the woman's lineal ascendants and descendants (mothers and daughters), but not to collateral relatives like sisters, based on a hadith from 'Imran ibn Husayn. The commentary also notes a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the extent of looking: Abu Yusuf considers looking at the hair roots sufficient, while Muhammad requires looking at the split (shiq); the relied-upon position is Muhammad's. The hadith is cited as evidence for the prohibition through fornication (zina) as well.

Key Terms
ممسوسة (mamsūsah): A woman whom a man has touched with desire, even if only her head hair or through a thin barrier.
ماسة (māssah): The woman who touches the man with desire; the text uses it similarly to mamsūsah in this ruling.
منظورة إلى فرجها الداخل (manẓūrah ilā farjihā al-dākhil): A woman whose internal private part (farj al-dakhil) is looked at with desire.
بشهوة (bi-shahwah): With sexual desire; must be present at the time of touch or look.
أصلهن (aṣluhunna): Their origins, i.e., the woman's lineal ascendants (mother, grandmother) and descendants (daughter, granddaughter) who become prohibited through musaharah or zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prohibition of marriage is established.
B) Prohibition of marriage is not established.
C) Prohibition is established only if the woman is reclining.
D) Prohibition is established only if he also looks at her private part.

Key Takeaway
Prohibition of marriage through musaharah is strict: it requires touch or look to the internal private part with desire at that moment, and only extends to the woman's lineal relatives.

Age of Desirability and Definition of Sexual Desire
Clarifies the age limit for desirability and defines shahwah for men and women.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the age of desirability and define shahwah for men and women.

Core Idea
A girl below nine is never desirable; shahwah is erection for men, inner desire for women.

This passage establishes a key legal threshold: girls below nine are legally not considered sexually desirable, which affects rulings on marriage prohibition after touch. It also defines shahwah (sexual desire) differently for men and women, resolving how to determine desire in each case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the age ruling
The text states that a girl below nine is not considered desirable (mushtahah). This is a fixed legal indicator.
This applies to any girl, regardless of actual physical maturity.
2
Understand the definition of shahwah
Shahwah is defined in two ways: inner desire (for both) and physical erection (for men). The correct position is that for men, erection or increase in erection is required.
For women, shahwah is only inner desire, as they lack the physical sign.
3
Distinguish between men and women
The passage explicitly differentiates: for women, shahwah is desire and pleasure; for men, the relied-upon definition is erection.
This distinction matters in legal proofs and claims.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some scholars defined shahwah as inner desire alone, but the author declares the erection-based definition as correct (sahih).
The mufta bihi according to this text is the erection-based definition.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If a man touches a girl under nine with no erection, no prohibition arises. If she is nine or older, shahwah must be verified per the definition.
Both age and correct definition must be satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما دون تسع سنين ليست بمشتهاة ، وبه يُفتى. اعلم أن بنت تسع سنين أو أكثر قد تكون مشتهاة أو لا، بخلاف ما دون تسع لا تكون مشتهاة قطعاً. واختلفوا في حد الشهوة: فعند البعض أن يشتهي بقلبه ويتلذذ به، وعند البعض أن ينتشر ذكره أو يزداد انتشاراً، وهو الصحيح. وأما في النساء لا يكون إلا هذا، أي الاشتهاء والتلذذ. وفي الرجال عند البعض أن ينتشر الذكر أو يزداد انتشاراً، هو الصحيح.
And a girl below nine years is not considered desirable, and this is the fatwa. Know that a girl of nine or more may or may not be desirable, unlike below nine where she is definitely not desirable. They differed on the definition of shahwah: some say it is desire in the heart and pleasurable sensation, and some say his penis becomes erect or increases in erection, and this is correct. As for women, it is only this, i.e., desire and pleasurable sensation. As for men, some say the penis becomes erect or increases in erection, and this is correct.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary on the matn 'What is below nine years is not desirable, and this is the fatwa.' It clarifies that a girl below nine years is legally considered not sexually desirable, so any touch or look without desire has no effect. The text then discusses the definition of shahwah (sexual desire). For men, the correct opinion is that shahwah is manifested by erection or increase of erection. For women, since that physical sign is not applicable, shahwah is defined as inner desire and pleasurable sensation. This distinction is important because the prohibition through musaharah depends on the presence of shahwah. The commentary notes that there is difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars, but the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that described above. The age ruling is a fixed legal rule that prevents any claim of shahwah for girls under nine.

Key Terms
مشتهاة (mushtahāh): A female who is sexually desirable; legally, a girl below nine years is not considered so.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire; for men, it is defined by erection or increase of erection; for women, by inner desire and pleasure.
انتشار الذكر (intishār al-dhakar): Erection of the penis; a physical sign of shahwah for men.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal definition of shahwah for a man?
A) Mere inclination of the heart.
B) Erection or increase of erection.
C) Any physical arousal.
D) Looking with desire.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a girl below nine is legally not desirable, and shahwah for men is defined by erection, while for women by inner desire.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate

The Age Threshold for Mahramiyyah: When is a Girl Considered Mushtahat?
Ruling with intra-madhhab ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a girl under nine becomes mahram through acts with shahwah, and distinguish between the three opinions on the definition of shahwah.

Core Idea
A girl under nine is never mushtahat; acts with shahwah do not create mahramiyyah.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh: the age and condition under which a female is considered 'mushtahat' (sexually desirable) for purposes of establishing mahramiyyah through looking or touching with shahwah. The matn declares that a girl under nine falls outside this category, and the commentary expands on the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the definition of shahwah and the age threshold. Understanding this ruling is crucial for determining when interactions between potential in-laws create prohibitions in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Ruling
Read the matn: 'وما دون تسع سنين ليست بمشتهاة، وبه يفتى'. This states that a girl under nine is not mushtahat, and this is the operative fatwa.
2
Analyze the Definition of Mushtahat
Examine the commentary: a girl of nine or more may be mushtahat depending on physique; below nine she is never mushtahat. This is the relied-upon position.
The commentary resolves the apparent conflict by noting that size matters for girls nine and above.
3
Map the Ikhtilaf on Shahwah
Three opinions are given on what constitutes shahwah: (1) physical arousal (erection for men, pleasure for women) without ejaculation; (2) emotional inclination and desire for intercourse; (3) no physical requirement for looking at the private part. Identify which is the mufta bihi.
The text states 'وبه يفتى' for the third opinion regarding looking at the private part, but the first opinion is attributed to the commentator and considered verified.
4
Understand the Age Dispute for Girls 5-9
There is a second ikhtilaf: one opinion holds a fixed age of nine; another considers physique for girls between five and nine. Determine the tarjih.
The text says 'والأصح أنها لا تثبت الحرمة' meaning that for girls between five and nine, the correct view is that prohibition (mahramiyyah) is not established, aligning with the primary ruling.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Consider a man who looks at a seven-year-old girl with shahwah as defined by each opinion. Determine whether mahramiyyah is established according to each view.
This step consolidates the thamarah al-khilaf from the madhhab dispute map.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما دون تسع سنين ليست بمشتهاة، وبه يفتى، اعلم أن بنت تسع سنين، أو أكثر، قد تكون مشتهاة، وقد لا تكون، وهذا يختلف بعظم الجنة وصغرها، أما قبل أن تبلغ تسع سنين، فالفتوى على أنها ليست بمشتهاة، اختلفوا في حد الشهوة على أقوال: الأول: ما ذكره الشارح وصححه، ويكون هذا إذا لم ينزل، فلو أنزل مع مس أو نظر فلا حرمة، والثاني: أن يميل قلبه إليها ويشتهي جماعها، وهو قول كثير من المشايخ، والثالث: لا يشترط في النظر للفرج تحريك آلته، وبه يفتى، كذا في «الجواهر»، وبنت تسع فصاعداً مشتهاة اتفاقاً، وفيما بين الخمس والتسع اختلاف الرواية والمشايخ، والأصح أنها لا تثبت الحرمة، اختلفوا في حد المشتهاة على قولين: الأول: إن ما دون تسع سنين ليست بمشتهاة وبنت التسع قد تكون مشتهاة وقد تكون لا، وبه أفتى أبو الليث وعليه يفتى كما ذكر المصنف والشارح وصاحب «الملتقى» و«الدر المختار» و«فتح باب العناية» وصححه صاحب «المعراج»، والثاني: إن بنت خمس لا تكون مشتهاة اتفاقاً، وبنت تسع فصاعداً مشتهاة اتفاقاً، وبنت ثمان أو سبع أو ست إن كانت ضخمة مشتهاة وإلا فلا، قاله أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل، قال الشمني وعليه الفتوى.
And a girl under nine years is not sexually desired, and this is the fatwa. Know that a girl of nine years or more may be desired or may not be, and this varies according to her size and smallness. As for before she reaches nine years, the fatwa is that she is not desired. They differed on the definition of desire on several opinions: first: what the commentator mentioned and verified, and this is if he does not ejaculate, for if he ejaculates by touch or look, there is no prohibition. Second: that his heart inclines to her and he desires intercourse with her, which is the saying of many scholars. Third: it is not required for looking at the private part to move his organ, and this is the fatwa. And a girl of nine and above is desired by agreement, and between five and nine there is difference in narration and among scholars, and the correct view is that prohibition is not established. They differed on the definition of desired woman on two opinions: first: that a girl under nine is not desired and a girl of nine may be desired or not, and Abu al-Layth gave fatwa on this and it is the fatwa. Second: that a girl of five is not desired by agreement, and a girl of nine and above is desired by agreement, and a girl of eight, seven, or six if she is large then she is desired otherwise not, said by Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, al-Shamni said this is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the legal definition of 'mushtahat' (a sexually desirable female) and its implications for mahramiyyah (prohibited relationships in marriage). The matn states that a girl under nine years of age is not mushtahat, and this is the operative fatwa. The commentary clarifies that a girl of nine may or may not be mushtahat depending on her physique, but before nine she is definitely not. The passage then records an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the definition of shahwah (sexual desire) itself, which is the standard for establishing mahramiyyah through acts like looking or touching. Three opinions are given: the first requires physical arousal (erection for men or pleasure for women) and absence of ejaculation if the act is to create prohibition; the second suffices with emotional inclination; the third does not require physical arousal for looking at the private part. The relied-upon position is the first. Another ikhtilaf concerns the age threshold: one opinion sets a fixed age of nine, while another considers physique for girls between five and nine. The text declares the first opinion as the fatwa. This discussion is crucial for determining when contacts between potential in-laws become mahram.

Key Terms
مشتهاة (mushtahat): A female who is sexually desirable, such that acts of looking or touching with shahwah establish mahramiyyah.
شهوة (shahwah): Sexual desire, defined differently for men (erection) and women (pleasure).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa, what is the ruling for a girl under nine years of age regarding becoming a mahram?
A) She is considered mushtahat and causes mahramiyyah.
B) She is not considered mushtahat, so no mahramiyyah.
C) It is disputed, but the stronger view is she is mushtahat.
D) She is only mushtahat if she has reached puberty.

Key Takeaway
A girl under nine is never mushtahat; thus, acts with shahwah do not establish mahramiyyah—a fixed age threshold that simplifies the ruling.

Nikah — Marriage
beginner
