Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage and Intercourse
Ruling on prohibition of combining two sisters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited ways of combining two sisters and identify the exception for mere ownership without intercourse.

Core Idea
Combining two sisters in marriage, iddah, or intercourse is haram, but ownership without intercourse is permitted.

This passage from al-Wiqayah clarifies a key prohibition in family law. Combining two sisters is absolutely forbidden in three specific scenarios. The commentary explains the legal reasoning and the proof from hadith, highlighting that the prohibition applies to intercourse, not to mere ownership of slave-girls.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'combining two sisters' (al-jam' bayn al-ukhtayn) in specific ways. The ruling is haram (prohibited) in three contexts: marriage, iddah, and intercourse with slave-girls.
The prohibition is absolute and agreed upon by all madhhabs.
2
Differentiate the three prohibited types
Marriage: marrying both sisters simultaneously. Iddah: marrying one while the other is in her iddah (even from a revocable or irrevocable divorce). Intercourse: having intercourse with both sisters as slave-girls (milk al-yamin).
The iddah has legal resemblance to marriage, hence the prohibition.
3
Note the exception for ownership
Mere ownership of two sisters as slaves without intercourse is permissible. The prohibition is limited to intercourse, not ownership itself.
The hadith mentions 'combining water in wombs', indicating intercourse.
4
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.' It is a weak hadith in chain but supported by consensus (ijma).
The Hanafi school accepts the ruling due to consensus despite weak chain.
5
Recognize the consensus
All scholars agree on the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage and intercourse; the only disputed point is mere ownership, which is allowed.
This is a muttafaq alayh ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجمع بين الأختين نكاحاً وعدة ولو من بائن، ووطئاً بملك يمين [١] قوله : نكاحاً أو عدة ; تمييزان من الجمع، ووجه حرمة الجمع عدة : أن للعدة ولو كانت من طلاق بائن حكم النكاح من وجه. [٢] قوله : بملك يمين ; متعلّق بالوطء واحترز به عن الجمع ملكاً بملك يمين من غير وطء، فهو جائز إنّما الممنوع وطؤهما يدلُّ عليه حديث: «مَن كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يجمعن ماءه في رحم أختين»(٢).
And combining two sisters in marriage, or during iddah even if from irrevocable divorce, and by intercourse through right hand possession. [1] His statement: in marriage or iddah – are specifications of the combination, and the reason for prohibition of combining through iddah is that the iddah, even if from irrevocable divorce, has the status of marriage in one respect. [2] His statement: through right hand possession – is related to intercourse and he guarded against combining through mere ownership without intercourse, for that is permitted; only intercourse with both is prohibited, as indicated by the hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day should not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.'
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage or by intercourse. The matn states that it is forbidden to combine two sisters in marriage (meaning simultaneously), during their iddah periods (even if the iddah is from an irrevocable divorce), or by having intercourse with both as slave-girls (milk al-yamin). The commentary explains the terms: 'nikahan' (in marriage) and 'iddatan' (during iddah) are two types of combination that are prohibited. The reason combining through iddah is prohibited is that the iddah period has a legal resemblance to marriage in terms of respect and honor. For milk al-yamin, the prohibition applies to intercourse, not mere ownership; it is permitted to own two sisters as concubines, but one cannot have intercourse with both. The proof is a hadith that prohibits mixing one's semen in the wombs of two sisters. The commentary notes that this hadith is weak in chain but the ruling is established by consensus of the scholars.

Key Terms
الجمع بين الأختين (al-jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): The act of combining two sisters in marriage or by intercourse during their iddah periods or through ownership.
ملك يمين (milk al-yamin): Ownership of a female slave, which allows intercourse without marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prohibited regarding combining two sisters?
A) Marrying both simultaneously.
B) Marrying one while the other is in an irrevocable iddah.
C) Having intercourse with both as slave-girls.
D) Owning two sisters as slaves without intercourse.

Key Takeaway
Combining two sisters is haram in three ways, but ownership without intercourse is allowed.
